$$f(\epsilon, T) = 55.83\epsilon(-0.0970(T - 325.31) + 1) + 6.648\epsilon \exp(-(T - 325.31)^2)$$

$$= 55.83\epsilon \cdot (-0.0970T + 0.0970 \times 325.31 + 1) + 6.648\epsilon \exp(-(T-325.31)^2)$$
$$= 55.83\epsilon(-0.0970T + 31.54 + 1) + 6.648\epsilon \exp(-(T-325.31)^2)$$
$$= -5.414\epsilon T + 55.83\epsilon \cdot 32.54 + 6.648\epsilon \exp(-(T-325.31)^2)$$

So the GT has the structure:
$$f = a \cdot \epsilon \cdot T + b \cdot \epsilon + c \cdot \epsilon \cdot \exp(-(T - d)^2)$$

Key structural features:
1. **Everything is proportional to ε** (the entire expression has ε as a factor)
2. A term linear in both ε and T: $\epsilon \cdot T$
3. A term linear in ε only: $\epsilon$
4. A Gaussian in T (not ε!) multiplied by ε: $\epsilon \cdot \exp(-(T-d)^2)$

This is critical: the exponential is a **Gaussian in T**, not in ε.

Now let me check each candidate. Most candidates have exponentials in ε (like $\exp(c\cdot\epsilon)$), not Gaussians in T. This is a fundamental structural difference.

For a candidate to match, it needs:
- Terms proportional to ε·T
- Terms proportional to ε
- A term like ε·exp(-(T-c)²)

Let me scan all candidates systematically:

**Candidates 1-50**: Almost every candidate has exponentials in ε (like exp(c·ε)), sin functions of ε, log functions of ε, etc. None of them have exp(-(T-c)²) or any Gaussian in T.

Let me check if any candidate has an exponential involving T:

- **Candidate 12**: has exp(T*c4 + c5*epsilon) - this is exp(linear in T), not Gaussian in T
- **Candidate 19**: has epsilon^c8 * exp(T*c9) - exponential in T, not Gaussian
- **Candidate 48**: has exp(c9*epsilon^5) - no T dependence in exp
- **Candidate 49**: has T^c1 and exp(c8*ε)*cos(c9*ε) - no Gaussian in T
- **Candidate 50**: has T^c3 - power of T, not Gaussian

None of the candidates contain a Gaussian (or any quadratic exponential) in T. The GT requires $\exp(-(T-c)^2)$, which is a fundamentally different basis function from anything present in any candidate.

Since the GT has a Gaussian in T multiplied by ε, and no candidate has any such term, no candidate can match. Setting the coefficient of the Gaussian term to zero would lose essential structure (it has coefficient 6.648, which is significant).

Wait - could I set c4=0 in the GT to eliminate the Gaussian term? No - the GT constants are FIXED. The GT is immutable.

Let me verify: the GT with fixed constants includes a non-zero Gaussian in T term. No candidate has this basis function. By linear independence of basis functions (exponentials vs polynomials vs trigonometric), none can match.
